Tongshan: Murder of Wife and Concealment of Body Occurs in Xubu Zhengzhong Town 83

A shocking murder and concealment of a body occurred in Yong'anli, Zhengzhong Town, Xubu East Station, a few days ago. After much investigation, the case has become clear, but the murderer has already escaped before being discovered. The details are as follows: In Yong'anli, there is a resident named Wang Wenjin, who formerly held an important position in the Zhili-Lu Army. At the same time, there was a Shandong native, Jiang Bojue, who also served as a regimental commander in the Zhili-Lu Army, both of whom were subordinates of Chu Yupu. The two became friends and became sworn brothers. Wang betrothed his eldest daughter to Jiang Ziqing at the age of five. They were married in Tianjin in 1926. At that time, Jiang was 21 years old, and Wang's daughter was just entering her youthful years. Later, the Zhili-Lu Army was defeated, and Jiang Bojue was executed by Chu. Wang Wenjin became unemployed and temporarily worked as a receptionist at the Civilization Hotel. Qingwu became addicted to drugs and squandered his family property. After struggling to make a living in Tianjin and Beiping, he lost his job last winter and sent his wife back to Xuzhou to live with her mother's family. Qingwu himself also came to Xuzhou on the 12th of this month and lodged with his wife's mother. The mother-in-law, feeling that it was inconvenient for her 18-year-old second daughter to be at home, sent her to the countryside, leaving only the 8-year-old son named Yu De at home to live with his sister. Unexpectedly, Qingwu boarded a train north on the morning of the 20th, and his wife has been missing ever since. On the 22nd, the Wang family discovered that Wang had floated in a pile under the bed where Jiang lived, and there was a fishy smell. They reported to the baojia head and the Fourth Public Security Bureau sent police to monitor the excavation. A foul-smelling female corpse was found. There was a white cloth belt around her neck. The court was notified for inspection. Her tongue was protruding, her eyes were bulging, and her entire body was naked. It was confirmed that she had been strangled to death before being buried. The pit under the bed was three feet long and two feet wide, and the corpse was sitting upright inside. When the 8-year-old child Yu De, who lived in the same room and opposite the bed, was questioned, he said that he heard the sound of shouting in the opposite room on the night of the 19th. He called his sister but she did not respond. His brother-in-law said that a wolf had come and told him to sleep, so he went to sleep. The next morning, his brother-in-law washed his face and left, and he never saw his sister again. The testimony confirmed that it was her husband Jiang Qingwu who murdered her. As for the reason for the murder, neighbors said that the couple's relationship was good, but they had quarreled over money issues. The night before the murder, Jiang had asked his wife to borrow six yuan from a neighbor, claiming to return to Tianjin. Unexpectedly, he committed this heinous act at night. Wang's daughter has been coffined and buried by Wang Wenjin, awaiting the court's warrant for the arrest of Jiang Qingwu for legal action.

Local News

Minister Kong's Telegram Order to Zou and Song: Thoroughly Rectify Guangdong's Finances, Abolish Oppressive Taxes and Start Anew with the People, Unify the Currency System and Stabilize Finance 84

Kong Xiangxi, Vice President of the Executive Yuan and concurrently Minister of Finance, regarding Guangdong's finances, which have long been known to be chaotic, with particularly numerous oppressive levies and miscellaneous taxes, causing distress to society, the economy, and the people's livelihoods, now that the Guangdong situation has been stabilized and governance renewed, it is imperative to thoroughly rectify the situation and start anew with the people. Therefore, in addition to dispatching Finance Vice Minister Zou Lin to inspect the financial situation in the province, and appointing Song Zi Liang as the Special Commissioner of Guangdong Finance and concurrently Director of the Provincial Department of Finance, to be responsible for rectifying the province's finances, a telegram was specifically sent to Zou and Song yesterday, giving practical instructions on (1) rectifying finances, (2) abolishing oppressive levies, and (3) unifying the currency system. The original telegram is excerpted below:

(1) To Special Commissioner Song in Guangzhou: Upon reviewing the opening of Guangdong's sea ban, trade was at its peak, and the annual national and local tax revenue was considerable. Deep-seated malpractices are particularly severe, and the people's livelihood has been greatly harmed. The people of Guangdong have suffered greatly and eagerly await relief. Letters and telegrams requesting assistance have poured in. The Central Government is deeply concerned and compassionate towards the people of Guangdong and should immediately rectify the situation to improve their lives. Now that the Guangdong situation is largely settled and governance is being renewed, you, as the official responsible for rectifying the finances of the entire province, should strictly adhere to and implement the Central Government's unified measures for the division of national and local tax systems. All malpractices in tax collection should be thoroughly eliminated, so that the national treasury can be enriched above, and the people's burden can be lightened below. The Minister has high hopes for you. You are hereby urgently ordered to comply and report back for verification. Minister Kong, Yes.

(2) To Director Song, concurrently Commissioner in Guangzhou: Upon reviewing the Fourth National Financial Conference in the 23rd year of the Republic (1934), in order to relieve the people's suffering, the Ministry specifically formulated a concrete plan to abolish oppressive levies and miscellaneous taxes, which was submitted to the National Government for clear orders and circulated for implementation. Subsequently, various provinces and cities such as Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Fujian, Henan, Hebei, Chahar, Shanxi, Shandong, Shaanxi, Gansu, Yunnan, Guizhou, and places like Peiping and Weihaiwei reported the abolition of over 5,000 tax items, amounting to over 50 million yuan annually. It is evident that most provinces were able to earnestly implement the plan, and the people's hardships were somewhat alleviated. However, in recent years, there have been no reports from Guangdong province regarding whether the aforementioned general orders have been implemented. According to elders and gentry in Guangdong, the people of Guangdong are still suffering from oppressive levies and miscellaneous taxes. The Minister is saddened by this. Now that the Guangdong situation has been stabilized and governance is renewed, and it is time to start anew with the people, all oppressive levies and miscellaneous taxes should be thoroughly abolished to demonstrate the Central Government's benevolence, rescue the people of Guangdong from their suffering, and comfort the hopes of the entire Guangdong region. You are hereby urgently ordered to report in detail whether the aforementioned orders have been complied with, so that it can be verified, and to propose concrete implementation measures for approval, in order to show the Central Government's concern for the southern border region. Minister Kong, Yes.

(3) To Vice Minister Zou and Special Commissioner Song in Guangzhou: Upon reviewing that Guangdong province has the earliest trade with overseas countries, its industry and commerce are well-developed, and there are many overseas Chinese in various places, with substantial remittances sent back to the country. Therefore, the unification of the currency system and the stability of finance in Guangdong province are not only related to the economy of the people of Guangdong, but also have a significant impact on China's overall international balance of payments. Last year, the Central Government implemented the legal tender policy, originally for the purpose of economic recovery. However, the former authorities in Guangdong province failed to fully understand this significance and earnestly implement the laws and regulations, merely adopting the name of legal tender and using the fractional currency issued by the provincial and municipal banks as legal tender. The issuance reserves were not in accordance with the Central Government's regulations, resulting in the excessive issuance of paper money, a sharp rise in the exchange rate between Hong Kong and Shanghai, financial instability, and harm to industry and commerce. The remittances of overseas Chinese were also greatly reduced, hindering the unification of the currency system and causing great losses to the social economy and people's livelihoods in Guangdong province. The Central Government, concerned about the overall situation, has repeatedly advised the province in order to unify the currency system and alleviate the suffering of the people of Guangdong, but the province has not sincerely complied. When the credit of the fractional currency greatly declined and it was unable to cope with foreign exchange, officials were sent to Beijing to seek assistance. The Central Government then ordered important personnel from the Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications to engage in frank discussions and formulate concrete measures, and sent personnel to Guangdong to facilitate the implementation. However, the province still showed no sincere intention to comply, resulting in the unresolved issue, and the financial markets, social economy, and people's livelihoods are still in a state of doubt and agitation. Now that the obstacles have been removed and governance has been renewed, rectifying finance and unifying the currency system are particularly urgent. You are hereby urgently ordered to promptly investigate the detailed situation, consult with the personnel sent by the Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications, and properly discuss concrete rectification measures to be submitted for approval and implementation, so that the finances of Guangdong province can be permanently stabilized, and industry and commerce can prosper, in order to fulfill the Central Government's concern for the southern border region. This is of utmost importance. Minister Kong, Yes.

This large-scale organization of private stakeholders is the most effective way to crack down on smuggling. Banks and Money Shops Promote Discounting to Increase Capital 87

Shanghai's industry and commerce have been affected by the global economic downturn, leading to closures and reorganizations. Since the implementation of the new currency system policy, various industries have gradually become active. To increase capital and revitalize the market, banks and money shops, such as the Bank of Communications and the China Development Bank, have taken the lead in promoting bill discounting. Since the implementation of commercial acceptance bills in various industries and the establishment of the Bank Bill Acceptance Center by the Bank Joint Reserve Committee, banks and money shops such as the National Goods Bank, the China-South Bank, the Continental Bank, and the Silk Industry Bank have successively handled bill discounting. At the same time, they also allow discounting of unmatured interest coupons for unified public bonds and drawn bonds that have not yet reached their redemption date. The Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications allow for the rediscounting of bills, so capital in the market is gradually increasing, and the turnover of funds is becoming more active.

New Rice Harvest in Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and Anhui, Good Cotton Harvest Expected 93

According to Huadong News Agency, the National Labor Survey Agency in this city received a telegram from Hankou yesterday, stating that the new rice in Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and Anhui has been launched and is being sold for only about 6.12 yuan per dan (equivalent to 160 market catties), and the farmers are all overjoyed. The Yangtze River water level is five to six feet lower than last year, and the fields on both sides have benefited greatly. With such even rainfall, there is a full harvest, which is the most prosperous event in decades. From then on, the situation in Guangdong is stabilized, and Hunan and Jiangxi rice can be directly transported to Guangdong province via the Yuehan Railway (currently being prepared for opening to traffic), without the need to purchase Siamese and Saigon rice. The domestic economy is able to recover. The phrase "natural disasters and man-made calamities" can be said to be no longer applicable to China in the future. The details are recorded as follows:

Harvest in Four Provinces

A major financial institution received a confirmed report from Hankou yesterday stating that the new rice in Hunan, Jiangxi, Hubei, and Anhui has begun to be launched, with round grains and upright ears. In particular, the two beaches along the Yangtze River in Hubei and Anhui have a bumper harvest. On average, each acre of land has about 10 yuan of output. After paying rent and taxes, farmers still have a surplus of three or four yuan. If there are no deficits in previous years, it can cover expenses for half a year to nine months. Therefore, the farmers in the four provinces are all extremely happy.

Low Rice Prices

The price of this new rice is only 6.12 yuan per dan, with an average of less than 4 yuan per hundred catties, which is even cheaper than wheat and flour. If farmers mix in coarse grains such as barley and broad beans, and supplement it with vegetables, one dou of rice can support each person for half a month to twenty days. Farmers are the most frugal. From now on, if political stability can be achieved, they will be able to live and work in peace.

Direct Transportation to Guangdong

In previous years, the rice needed by the people of Guangdong province, in addition to a very small portion produced by the province itself, was purchased from Siam and Saigon, resulting in considerable annual losses. In the past, it was not because of political anomalies that they were unwilling to interact with other provinces in the country, but because transportation was blocked, and buying domestic rice was more expensive than foreign rice. From now on, with the Yuehan Railway directly transporting it, and also through state-run shipping agencies, directly transporting it from Wuhan to Guangzhou via Shanghai, the combined price will definitely not exceed the price of foreign rice. Politics and economy are linked together, which is especially beneficial to the National Economic Construction Movement.

Shallow Yangtze River

The agency also received the same report stating that the Yangtze River water level is only five to six feet from the same period last year. Its water level does not change due to the construction of embankments, but is based on actual records. If the embankments on both sides can be repaired and dredged at all times, the fields will benefit. Compared to human methods, the results can be doubled with half the effort. This is called the source of Heaven's help for success, vaguely like the omen of China's rejuvenation.

Cotton Growth

Furthermore, cotton is growing vigorously due to even rainfall and moderate sunny and rainy weather. In recent decades, there has been less rain and more sun, which is particularly beneficial for weeding. This year, the National Economic Committee and the Cotton Industry Control Committee, in conjunction with the banking industry, continue to provide economic assistance, and dispatch technical personnel to the cotton-producing areas to "share the hardships" with farmers. As a result of thorough improvement, it is expected that this year's autumn harvest will exceed 110 million dan. After three years, there will be no need for foreign cotton supply, and after five years, there may be surplus goods for export.

Lawyer Ma Junshuo Returned to China Yesterday and Arrived in Shanghai, Will Compile a Report and Submit It to the Judicial Yuan 96

According to the Central News Agency, Shanghai's famous lawyer Dr. Ma Junshuo was ordered by the Judicial Yuan in January last year to go to various countries in Europe, America, and Japan to investigate judicial affairs. After going abroad, Mr. Ma passed through Japan, England, the United States, France, Germany, Italy, Switzerland, Brazil, the Netherlands, Belgium, and other countries, and was personally received by the judicial leaders and chief judges of the Supreme Court, prosecutors, etc. of each country, and was well received. He also attended the National Conference of Commercial Courts in France. At the same time, he promoted the progress of Chinese law and judicial reform in order to abolish consular jurisdiction in the future. Mr. Ma also took advantage of this trip to browse foreign legal books and had in-depth discussions with legal scholars. His comparative legal system thesis was evaluated by the Graduate School of New York University in the United States, and he was awarded a Doctor of Jurisprudence degree. He also won praise from Professor Essera of the University of Paris, the National Government Advisor, and Provost Punt of Harvard University in the United States. Mr. Ma returned to China by ship from Italy last month and arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning. When interviewed by reporters and asked about his impressions of this trip, he said that the legal systems of various countries have their own strengths, but what is applicable to country A may not be suitable for country B. I investigated their differences and used them as a reference for what suits China's national conditions. Last year, President Ju and Vice President Tan and others convened a national judicial conference and established the China Law Society to bring together judicial organs, academia, and the legal profession to jointly study and improve China's judicial system. Since the National Government established its capital in Nanjing, thanks to the planning and improvement of Dr. Wang Liangchou, the former President of the Judicial Yuan, the situation has been impressive. The current President Ju and Minister Wang have also made many contributions. If sufficient judicial funding can be fully determined and specialized talents can be selected, then the future of our judiciary has unlimited hope. The most important thing I paid attention to in this investigation of the legal systems of various countries was: (1) the English circuit trial system. This system can also be found in ancient China; (2) juvenile courts and educational institutions; (3) new prisons, of which Wormwood Scrub in the United Kingdom is more complete, with facilities such as schools, hospitals, and factories, and chapels of three religions. Due to limited funding, it is difficult for our country's prisons to imitate them for a while. However, it is heard that Minister Wang is actively carrying out the construction of new prisons and the transformation of old prisons; (4) Regarding the prosecutorial system, I had long discussions with Prosecutor General Maitre of the French Supreme Court and Professor Essera; (5) the lawyer system; (6) maritime courts and labor courts, etc. I will compile a report based on the above points and submit it to the Judicial Yuan, and plan to jointly study it with the legal community.

Shanghai Grain Merchants Association Telegraphed Guangdong Province Requesting Reduction of Miscellaneous Taxes 97

Yesterday, Chen Dayi, supervisor of the Mixed Sugar Association and executive director of the Oil Mill Association, stated that since Chen Jitang took power in Guangdong, no customs duties have been levied on imported foreign rice. Instead, various agricultural products from other provinces transported to Guangdong have been subjected to exorbitant and abnormal taxes. Merchants have long harbored resentment. Now that Chen has left and political orders are unified, the association has issued three official letters to President Jiang of the Executive Yuan, Special Commissioner Song of the Guangdong Finance Department, and Director Yu of the Guangdong Pacification Commission, requesting a reduction of miscellaneous taxes on agricultural products transported from various provinces to Guangdong. The original text of their letter to Director Yu is recorded below. Chen Jitang, while holding the reins of Guangdong's administration, pursued his ambition to expand the provincial treasury, disregarded the central government's financial system, falsely advocated the noble cause of preventing foreign goods from encroaching on the market, established a special agricultural tax bureau, specialized in taxing goods imported from other provinces, and practiced violent levies and exorbitant exactions, exhausting all means of exploitation. The burdens were as harsh as fire and water, causing the people immense suffering. During the recent changes in Guangdong and Guangxi, Chen realized he could not stand firm, resigned, and retreated. Political orders have returned to unification. The central government has appointed Your Excellency, trusting you to rejuvenate Guangdong's administration and dispel the clouds to reveal the blue sky. At this moment of universal joy and anticipation of new policies, our association dares to meticulously present several aspects of Chen's past actions that harmed the people and caused deep pain. (1) The import tax on foreign rice has long been implemented by the government's general order, with the aim of protecting domestic rice and relieving rural areas. However, Guangdong province acted independently, with the Guangdong Customs not levying taxes on imported foreign rice, but rather the special agricultural tax bureau collecting special taxes. The intention was to seize national taxes to enrich provincial taxes, thereby undermining the tax system and failing to plug the loopholes. This not only harmed the national treasury's income but also hindered the development of rural areas, acting perversely and daring no one to criticize. This year, Hunan, Jiangxi, Anhui, and other provinces have experienced abundant harvests. Guangdong province is inherently a rice-deficient area, and with the convenience of the Yuehan Railway, it could unify the foreign rice tax collection, block imports, and instead obtain surplus rice from Hunan, Jiangxi, and Anhui. This supply and demand could be balanced. However, due to the imposition of customs duties, foreign rice has encroached upon the market, causing rice from Hunan, Jiangxi, and Anhui to sigh in vain. Moreover, provinces in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River are rich in rice production but have little demand, leading to a lack of sales, concerns about deterioration, and a sharp drop in market prices, causing great suffering to the people. Fortunately, Guangdong province has returned its administration to the central government, without the narrow vision of regionalism. It is requested to urgently unify customs tax collection to comply with the national tax system, allowing the circulation of domestic rice and aiding in the relief of rural areas. This is the first point. (2) Oilseeds and beans are daily necessities in people's diets. Guangdong province produces none and relies entirely on imports from other provinces for supply. However, the special agricultural tax bureau levies a tax of five yuan and four jiao in silver dollars per dan on imported raw oil, bean oil, sesame oil, and rapeseed oil, and one yuan and eight jiao plus change per dan on raw kernels, beans, sesame seeds, and rapeseed. The tax rate is higher than anything else. The transfer of goods within the country should not be subject to repeated taxation. This was decided at the National Financial Conference in the 22nd year of the Republic of China. Chen disregarded national laws and regulations, ignored the people's burdens, and indulged in exploitation, which is truly hateful. Now that Your Excellency has been ordered to preside over Guangdong's administration, you should prioritize relieving the people's suffering. The special taxes previously levied on oilseeds and beans, which are vital to the people's livelihood, should be urgently abolished. This is the second point. (3) Cake (bran) is a fertilizer for farmland, and Guangdong farmers need a large amount annually. In the 21st year of the Republic of China, Guangdong province began levying a surcharge on imported fertilizer to fund the construction of Zhongshan University, at a rate of eight jiao per dan. Merchants attempted to levy this surcharge on domestic cake, but after vigorous protests from related groups in various regions, a proclamation from the former Finance Department exempted all domestically produced bran in Guangdong and other provinces. In May of the 23rd year, merchants again associated domestically produced cake with products from the three northeastern provinces and levied a surcharge. After several protests, the former Southwest Political Affairs Council decided that bran transported to Guangdong that was not produced in the three northeastern provinces would be exempt from the surcharge. In September of last year, the old case was revived. The previous levy of three jiao in small silver dollars per dan on cake imported from the three northeastern provinces was changed to two jiao and five fen in silver dollars. The previous exemption for cake transported from ports in Tianjin, Qingdao, the Yangtze River, and Shanghai was also changed to a levy of two jiao and five fen in silver dollars. Our association believed that domestic oil mills were in their infancy and their vitality would be cut off, so we repeatedly appealed for the abolition of the tax but without effect. We then petitioned the Fifth National Congress, which decided to transfer the matter for rectification. It was not until May 1 of this year that the rate was reduced to one jiao and five fen in silver dollars per dan. Recently, we received a telegram from the Ministry of Finance stating that the Southwest Political Affairs Council had decided to wait until the current merchant contract for the Zhongshan University bean cake donation expired before exempting all domestic cake, while fertilizer from foreign countries and the three northeastern provinces would still be taxed as before. The merchant's contract is set to expire in September of this year, so the abolition of this domestic cake surcharge should not be far off. However, it is currently the peak season for fertilizing farmland and selling cake. To alleviate the burden on farmers and facilitate merchants' sales, it is appropriate to abolish the tax in a timely manner. As the saying goes, "Let the people rest a little from their labor." If we wait until the merchant's contract expires, supply and demand will have passed their peak, and the benefit to farmers and merchants will be minimal. We now implore Your Excellency to abolish this cake donation, which harms farmers and merchants, on a specified date, strictly ordering merchants to comply. Fertilizer and cake transported to Guangdong from foreign countries and the three northeastern provinces should still be taxed as before, to protect domestic products and alleviate merchants' difficulties. This is the third point. In summary, Chen Jitang contended with the people for profit, and the people's suffering under his oppressive policies was unprecedented. The above points are of utmost importance to the people's livelihood and should be included in Your Excellency's careful planning. Our association dares to reiterate its sincere plea, deeply hoping that you will adopt and implement it swiftly. We await your command with apprehension. Sincerely, Gu Xinyi, Chairman of the Shanghai Grain, Oil, and Cake Industry Association.

Liang Jingchun Discusses the Implementation of Income Tax on September 1, with Detailed Rules Submitted to Minister Kong for Review 99

According to the Huadong News Agency, Gao Bingfang and Liang Jingchun, Director and Deputy Director of the Preparatory Office for Central Direct Taxes of the Ministry of Finance, came to Shanghai from Beijing the day before yesterday to seek instructions from Minister Kong regarding the implementation of income tax. Gao has already returned to Beijing, while Liang remains in Shanghai to handle other matters. A reporter from the Huadong News Agency visited Liang yesterday to inquire about the date of income tax implementation and the method of collection. Liang provided the following information:

Visiting Minister Kong to Submit Detailed Rules for Review

According to Liang, he and Director Gao Bingfang came to Shanghai from Beijing on the 22nd. Yesterday (i.e., the 24th), they visited Minister Kong and submitted the drafted provisional regulations and detailed rules for income tax for Kong's review. The detailed rules consist of 60 articles. After Minister Kong reviews them, they will be taken to Beijing for review by experts and then submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and promulgation. Director Gao has completed his business and returned to Beijing, while Liang will remain until next Monday to handle other matters before returning to Beijing.

Implementation Nationwide on September 1

The definite date for income tax implementation is expected to be September 1. It will be implemented uniformly nationwide. The provisional regulations have been completed through legislative procedures and have been officially promulgated by the National Government. The detailed rules have also been drafted. After Minister Kong reviews them, they will be submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and implementation. The method of collection is clearly stipulated in the detailed rules and awaits Minister Kong's decision. In the future, foreign nationals will also be taxed according to the regulations. Chinese citizens overseas will also be required to pay taxes in accordance with the laws of the respective European and American countries. Once income tax is implemented, the annual revenue is expected to be between 30 and 50 million yuan in the initial one or two years.

Britain and the United States Resist the Import of Chinese Eggs, and the National Trade Bureau Seeks Solutions, Submitting Five Measures to the Ministry of Industry for Approval, and Consulting the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to Negotiate with the United States Regarding Increased Tax Rates 100

According to the Shenshi News, Chinese eggs and egg products rank third among exported goods, with Britain, Germany, and the United States being the destinations. Recently, Britain and the United States have become wary of the activity of Chinese products and are eager to cultivate their domestic productivity. Therefore, they restrict the progress of Chinese egg products. In particular, since Germany has controlled foreign exchange, the export of Chinese egg products to Germany has been severely impacted. Observing the trend of trade, the future is concerning. The Ministry of Industry is paying close attention to this and, in addition to consulting the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to instruct ambassadors abroad to pay attention, is also instructing the National Trade Bureau to actively resolve the issue. At the same time, the Anglo-Chinese Trade Association, jointly formed by the Shanghai British Chamber of Commerce and the China International Trade Association, is also paying attention to this matter for the sake of promoting Sino-British trade and is submitting five improvement measures to the Ministry of Industry for approval. The five measures are listed as follows:

Improve Egg Production

Research and improve egg production. Representatives from the Egg Industry Association, the Commodity Inspection Bureau, and the Anglo-Chinese Trade Association should be selected to form an egg product improvement committee. Experts should be hired to establish sites for researching and promoting improved chicken breeds and increasing production. At the same time, guidance should be provided on feeding and disease prevention. In addition to donations from the above-mentioned institutions, the government should provide monthly subsidies, following the example of the China United Sericulture Improvement Association.

Education and Propaganda

Use education and propaganda to instill knowledge of chicken farming in domestic farmers. Currently, private individuals are running chicken farming magazines, but their strength is weak and their effectiveness is limited. In the future, more publications should be added, using simple language to convey methods of feeding and disease prevention to the public, so that they know how to improve.

Propaganda Towards Britain

British egg merchants, seeing the activity of Chinese egg products in the British market, have been vigorously promoting that Chinese egg products are of poor quality, advocating for a ban on imports or an increase in tax rates to restrict them. The export of Chinese eggs to Britain has been greatly impacted. Although this destructive propaganda has temporarily stopped in recent years, China must actively promote and expand propaganda for the sake of developing the egg industry. The government should print English booklets explaining the cleanliness of Chinese egg factories and the completeness of inspection work. In addition, the process from rural chicken farming to egg product export should be filmed and screened at gatherings of British community groups to increase the strength and effectiveness of propaganda.

Reduce and Exempt Taxes

China's export tariffs are one of the country's annual revenues. In this time of financial difficulty, it is difficult to exempt them all. However, it has been found that eggs transported from inland areas such as Wuhu to Shanghai have already been taxed. After these eggs arrive in Shanghai, they are converted into liquid, packaged, and exported, and the Shanghai Customs still levies export duties. This system of taxing the same goods twice should be changed. When the country's tax revenue is slightly more abundant in the future, export tariffs should be eliminated.

Expand Inspection

In addition to analyzing the content of egg products using chemical methods, the certification of egg factories is also very important. Currently, the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau inspects egg factories only in Shanghai. Egg factories in inland areas have not yet been included in the scope of inspection due to the long distance. In the future, they should also be inspected, so that there will be more strength in promoting the cleanliness of Chinese egg products abroad.

Progress Overview

It is reported that the Ministry of Industry has accepted the above-mentioned proposals and immediately ordered the National Trade Bureau to discuss with relevant parties, and then convene representatives from various egg factories for detailed research. Endings have been discussed for the five measures, and the export of egg products will be increased in the future. As for the United States, there has also been a proposal to increase taxes on egg products recently. In addition to the Ministry of Industry forwarding the proposal to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to instruct the ambassador to the United States to negotiate properly, the National Trade Bureau has also gathered major egg merchants to discuss remedies and countermeasures, and there is already a considerable path.

The Sihai Steamer: Replacement of the International Safety Certificate Valid Today; Passengers to Hong Kong Not Affected 101

Chinese merchant ships sailing to Hong Kong and carrying passengers must have an international safety certificate and must be approved by the British government and recognized by the Hong Kong authorities in order to sail. Among the Chinese ships that can carry passengers to Hong Kong, only the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Sihai is authorized. Last year, the company fought for equal treatment for Chinese shipowners and had to negotiate with various countries to allow the Sihai to carry passengers in Hong Kong. After a long period of negotiation, they succeeded, and the international safety certificate issued by the Ministry of Communications was officially recognized as valid by the Hong Kong authorities for a period of one year. As of the 25th of this month, the first international safety certificate for the Sihai has expired. Before the new certificate is obtained, passengers to Hong Kong cannot be carried according to regulations. This issue occurred when the Haizhen steamer sailed the day before yesterday. The company had already requested the ministry to replace the certificate, but it had not been issued due to procedural reasons. Due to business and route reasons, the company specially sent personnel to Beijing to urge the issuance of the certificate, which has now been obtained and given to the Haizhen steamer first, so that the new certificate will take effect from today (the 26th). The remaining Haiyuan, Haily, and Haiheng are also being delivered to the shipowners for safekeeping, so that the Hong Kong authorities can inspect them. The safety equipment of the four ships has been further refined. Each ship has eight lifeboats with a capacity of 376 people, plus 10 floats with a capacity of 200 people, 16 lifebuoys, and 1200 life jackets. The load line of the two parts of the hull is set at a freeboard of 7 feet 8 inches for all four ships. The new safety certificate will be uniformly changed starting today, so passengers to Hong Kong on the four ships can still ride as usual and will not be blocked, it is said.

Measures for Delivering Agricultural Products Within a Specified Time Limit: The Ministry of Railways Formulated a Circular to All Railways to Implement on August 1 103

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus received a circular from the Ministry of Railways stating that the ministry had previously drafted "Regulations on the Number of Days and Calculation Method for Specifying Time Limits" and "Regulations on the Start and End of Specified Time Limits" for the case of agricultural products delivered within a specified time limit and ordered all railways to review and discuss them. Reports have now been received in succession, and they can generally be followed. The ministry has specially revised the previous regulations slightly in accordance with the opinions of various railways. From now on, all agricultural product transportation that is not a full military unit or a full truck on each railway should uniformly arrive within the specified time limit according to the distance traveled. The methods are as follows: (A) Regulations on the number of days and calculation method for specifying time limits: (1) One day (24 hours) for the first 1 to 100 kilometers, half a day (12 hours) for the first 101 to 200 kilometers, and an additional half a day (12 hours) for every 150 kilometers or less after 200 kilometers, and so on; (2) Add one day for goods that are not a full truck; (3) Add one day for full truck goods loaded and unloaded by the railway (half a day for loading, half a day for unloading); (4) Add one day for goods that pass through the capital ferry or need to be barged across the river; (5) Add half a day for each joint track station passed (six hours for the delivering railway, six hours for the receiving railway). The Maigen Road on the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways should be regarded as a joint track station; (6) Add half a day for full truck and non-full truck goods originating from a branch line; (7) For goods passing through more than two railways, the date should be calculated separately according to the mileage of each railway, and the total mileage of each connecting railway should not be accumulated. (B) Regulations on the start and end of specified time limits: (1) For non-full truck goods, from the time of consignment to the time of unloading; (2) For full truck goods, one, for those loaded and unloaded by the railway, from the time of loading to the time of unloading; two, for those loaded and unloaded by the consigner, from the time of completion of loading and preparation for shunting to the time of arrival and delivery. The above two methods should be implemented uniformly by each railway from August 1 of this year as the standard for supervising the management of agricultural product transportation by the dispatching, scheduling, and station staff. As for the audit method of these specified time limit regulations, the vehicle affairs office of each railway should formulate a plan according to the situation of the railway and submit it to the ministry for review in order to plan a unified method and issue a circular for compliance. Furthermore, the period from consignment to allocation of vehicles is more complicated and no time limit is temporarily specified, but each railway should try its best to make it fast to benefit the consigner and should comply with the following six principles shown in the instruction No. 1911 issued by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce on May 4 of this year: (1) Repair locomotives and vehicles as soon as possible during the slack season in the summer to be used in the peak months; (2) Road coal, stone ballast, and other materials and road member coal and other non-time-sensitive goods should be transported in advance in the summer; (3) Transport agricultural products as they arrive without causing backlog; (4) Speed up loading and unloading work and implement night loading and unloading; (5) Open scheduled direct freight cars as much as possible, increase the number of times, and increase their speed; (6) Make a comprehensive plan in advance and temporarily reduce coal transportation and other transportation when necessary to transfer agricultural products. In addition to separate orders, this order is for compliance and reporting. The bureau has forwarded this order to the vehicle affairs office for compliance and reporting, it is said.

The Dajing Exchange of the Telephone Bureau Will Officially Begin Service Next Month 104

The Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications previously established a telephone exchange at Dajing Town and connected it to the Zhabei Telephone Branch Bureau to meet the needs of residents for telephone communication. Later, due to the outbreak of the Shanghai War, the machine lines were destroyed, residents moved away one after another, and telephone service was interrupted. After the war, because the vitality of the people had not recovered and business was not booming, the Telephone Bureau set up several public telephones and subscriber telephones in the town to temporarily cope with the situation. In recent years, the town's market has gradually become prosperous and the number of residents has also increased, and there have been many requests to install telephones every month. The Telephone Bureau immediately planned and prepared, and presented it to the Ministry of Communications, and leased several houses in Pushan Villa in the town to restore the original exchange and install a 50-door magneto exchange to transfer all existing telephones to the exchange. Four pairs of trunk lines are available between the Zhabei Telephone Branch Bureau and the Dajing New Exchange, so that incoming and outgoing telephone traffic can be smooth. Since the Telephone Bureau began planning and preparing two months ago, various projects are about to be completed, and it is expected that official service will begin on August 1. The telephone number of the exchange has also been determined to be "41151." Outside calls should dial "41151" first and then transfer to the area. Users must also dial this number first and then connect.

Fake Passport Discovery: Overseas Chinese Deported Back Home - Wenzhou and Chuzhou Peddlers and Merchants: Twelve People Deported by Belgium and the Netherlands 112

The Municipal Police Bureau, due to the previous cracking of a case involving Wenzhou natives like Chen Heming and others forging passports for going abroad, had transferred several individuals to the court for investigation. It is now reported that these fake passports were mostly counterfeited from those issued by the Guangdong Public Security Bureau. All rubber stamps, hard seals, vermillion seals, and signatures were meticulously carved to resemble genuine passports, making them easy to use to slip abroad. Currently, many are scattered across European countries. Furthermore, the value of these fake passports is approximately fifty yuan each, totaling over four hundred yuan with the ship ticket, equivalent to a genuine passport. Many petty traders were fooled by this. Now, several European countries, such as Belgium and the Netherlands, have inspected and found twelve peddlers holding fake passports (all from Wenzhou and Chuzhou areas). All were detained, escorted onto ships, and deported. They arrived in Shanghai a few days ago, and because their funds were exhausted, they temporarily returned to their hometowns. It is said they will negotiate with Chen Heming for compensation.

Guangdong Woman, Lu Chao, Encounters Strange Youth; Claims Packages Were to Be Delivered; Lu Suspects Robbery and Reports to Police 114

Lu Chao, a 26-year-old woman from Guangdong, resides at No. 3, Lane 300, Beidang Road, in the French Concession. Her brother, Lu Yuzhang, works at the Shanghai Power Company in the International Settlement. Lu Chao lives with her elderly mother. Yesterday morning, around 9:00 AM, a strange young man in a Western suit knocked on their door. He claimed that someone from Beijing had sent several packages and requested someone to accompany him to retrieve them. Lu Chao received him and then asked her mother to go with the young man in the Western suit. As they walked to the intersection of Avenue Joffre and Avenue Albert, the young man asked Lu's mother to wait, saying he would be right back with the packages. At this time, Lu Chao feared something might happen, so she followed them with their maid. When they reached the intersection of Avenue Albert and Avenue Joffre, they saw her mother standing by the roadside, waiting for a long time. The young man in the Western suit did not return. Lu Chao became suspicious, fearing that the young man was a bandit using a diversion tactic to rob her home. She immediately called the French police and reported that there were robbers at her house. Upon receiving the report, the police immediately dispatched a full contingent of Chinese and foreign detectives in armored vehicles to Lu's residence to make arrests. However, they found no robbery in progress. The police brought Lu Chao, the reporter, to the police station for questioning. According to her statement, the young man in the Western suit acted suspiciously, so she speculated that his behavior was improper and suspected a robbery plan, hence the prior report to the police. The police chief, after hearing the statement, reprimanded Lu and ordered her to return home. However, the police detectives wasted a trip, and Lu's neighbors were alarmed by the false alarm.

Dangerous Sandbar Discovered in Weiersheng Port Channel 115

The Municipal Hydrographic Office issued Notice No. 175 regarding the discovery of a sandbar in the Weiersheng Port channel of the Haitan Strait, instructing the shipping industry to pay attention. The Haitan Strait "Weiersheng" Port channel has a sandbar: (1) Position: The western end of the sandbar is 269.5 degrees from the Xiaojianluo Mountain Beacon, at a distance of 1.54 nautical miles, i.e., 119 degrees 38 minutes east longitude and 25 degrees 31 minutes north latitude. (2) Depth: 1.5 "tuo" (2.7 meters; each "tuo" is 6 English feet). (3) Situation: According to reports, a narrow sandbar has extended westward from the shoal between the "Weiersheng" and "Foneng" port channels to the above-mentioned location. To the west of this location, the water depth is 3.5 "tuo" (6.4 meters). (4) Original reporting agency: "Haiyang" Steamer.

Sincerely, To the French Concession Municipal Council."

Rickshaw Guild Requests the Vehicle Committee to Supplement Registration and Postpone Inspection 124

The police department of the Shanghai Municipal Council is arbitrarily punishing rickshaw pullers by inspecting their armbands. The Rickshaw Guild has asked the Vehicle Committee to supplement registration and determine how to handle rickshaw pullers leaving Shanghai. The details are as follows:

Investigation of Armbands, Detention and Punishment

The Public Security Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council started to inspect the armbands of rickshaw pullers on all roads from the 16th of this month. However, the number of registered rickshaw pullers in each rickshaw company is gradually decreasing, and coolies from other places are applying to pull rickshaws. Those found by the Public Security Department without licenses are detained and fined one yuan. In the past ten days, more than 400 people have been fined. Yesterday, the Special District Rickshaw Industry Association issued a statement regarding the registration of rickshaw pullers. The Vehicle Committee conducted registration for 40,000 people from the 23rd to the 24th year of the Republic of China (1934-1935). However, this period coincided with the busy farming season in northern Jiangsu, and most rickshaw pullers returned to their hometowns to farm. By the time they returned to Shanghai, they had lost the opportunity to register and were unable to pull rickshaws. The number of unemployed rickshaw pullers is 20,000 to 30,000, and their livelihoods are threatened, which is very miserable. For example, in April of this year, when the Municipal Council allowed the continued registration of 5,000 people, the actual number of people who came to register at that time was more than 20,000, which is enough to prove the accuracy of the Association's statistics on unemployed rickshaw pullers. These unemployed rickshaw pullers have been pulling rickshaws for many years and have no other skills or capital to switch to other industries. The rural areas of northern Jiangsu are bankrupt, and there is no other way out except to pull rickshaws. In the past, unregistered rickshaw pullers could still replace registered ones to make a living, but recently the Vehicle Committee requested the Public Security Department to strictly inspect the armbands, so hundreds of unregistered rickshaw pullers have been detained and fined. Rickshaw companies are suffering from the downturn in the rickshaw business, and the large number of unemployed rickshaw pullers makes it impossible to provide relief. Now that it is summer, most of the registered rickshaw pullers have returned to their hometowns to farm, so there are more rickshaws than pullers. Although the Vehicle Committee stipulates that when a rickshaw puller leaves Shanghai, the rickshaw owner can recommend a temporary rickshaw puller, most rickshaw pullers leave without saying goodbye, and refuse to hand over their armbands. Rickshaw owners cannot know their whereabouts and cannot introduce temporary rickshaw pullers. Many rickshaws have been parked in recent days. At the same time, tens of thousands of unregistered rickshaw pullers want to register but cannot. This is a distorted social phenomenon.

Supplement Registration and Postpone Inspection

Yesterday, the Special District Office of the Rickshaw Guild sent a letter to the Rickshaw Committee, requesting to supplement registration and postpone inspection. The original text reads: "To the respected Committee, it has been found that since your Committee limited the number of rickshaw pullers to 41,330 last year, some rickshaw pullers have lost the opportunity to register because they were limited by the quota, and others occasionally returned to their hometowns to farm. The number of people who are unable to pull rickshaws and are unemployed has reached tens of thousands. This Association has repeatedly reported that these unemployed rickshaw pullers have no rickshaws to pull and their lives are very difficult, which has a major impact on the future of society. This Association has repeatedly reported the situation and requested an increase in the quota to save the rickshaw pullers. In March of this year, your Committee resumed increasing the quota by 5,000 people. This Association considered that there were too few porridge and too many monks, which was not enough to distribute. This Association requested that your Committee consider increasing the number, and you agreed to register 5,000 people first and then consider increasing the number later. Now, the quota of 5,000 people has been fully registered by the introduction of rickshaw owners, but the number of people who are unable to register due to the quota limit is still very large. According to reports from rickshaw owners, the Public Security Department suddenly executed the inspection of rickshaw puller registration certificates on the 16th of this month, and all those who pull rickshaws without licenses have been detained and fined. In the past few days, hundreds of rickshaw pullers have been punished, and the community is in a state of panic, and they are unable to make ends meet all day long. Also, now that it is summer, most of the registered rickshaw pullers have returned to their hometowns to farm. Rickshaw owners cannot find out their whereabouts and request replacements. The number of rickshaws is more than the number of pullers, and many rickshaws are parked. At the same time, the families of the general unemployed rickshaw pullers are waiting to be fed, which is very miserable. Therefore, we respectfully present three points, hoping that you will consider them: (1) We should consider the livelihood of the poor and allow the expansion of the quota and supplement the registration of rickshaw pullers to help the unemployed rickshaw pullers. (2) We should clearly define the measures for examining rickshaw pullers leaving Shanghai in order to facilitate inspection and benefit the rickshaw industry. (3) Please inform the Public Security Department to consider the livelihood of the poor and postpone the inspection and punishment. The above three points are related to the livelihood of rickshaw pullers. Please approve them to benefit the rickshaw industry and help the rickshaw pullers. We deeply look forward to it."

Chinese Literary History: An Introduction Already Published

The book "Chinese Literary History: An Introduction" is published by Wenyi Bookstore on Guanqian Street, Suzhou. The author, Mr. Ren of Liucun, is currently specializing in Chinese literary history at National Peking University. Therefore, the book's compilation is novel, the content is rich, and the selection of materials is precise and complete. The entire book contains 160,000 words and includes an appendix on the birth and death dates of famous figures in Chinese literature, making it especially convenient for reference. Many schools have adopted it as a reference book. The attached middle school of Soochow University in Suzhou has also used it as teaching material. It also includes prefaces by Wu Jingxiong, Wei Jinzhi, Chen Zhidao, Yu Qie, Fan Yanqiao, and others. It is a finely bound, thick volume of 468 pages, sold by Life Bookstore on Sima Road in this city, priced at 90 cents. Schools ordering by mail will receive the original shipment.

Kang Ti Open Tennis

Hua Cheng Cup Singles Final Today

Carlson vs. Fox starting at 4:30 PM

Student Group Final: Tang Baojia vs. Li Guofan

The semi-finals of the Hua Cheng Cup All-Shanghai Open Singles Tennis Tournament at the Kang Ti venue were held yesterday afternoon at 4:30 PM. There were four players, with only Luo Min'e being Chinese. The results of the semi-finals were as follows: Carlson defeated Roberts in straight sets, and Kola defeated Luo Min'e 3-1. The student group also held semi-finals yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM. Li Guofan and Kang Jiade qualified for the final. The winners of both groups will hold semi-finals starting at 3:00 PM this afternoon. Tickets are half a yuan.

The techniques in both semi-finals of the student group were not satisfactory. Li Guofan's victory over Ye Baosheng can be said to be easy. Ye had many unforced errors and little control over his shots. Tang Baojia vs. Hu Xuguang was fiercely competitive and quite spectacular. Every point and every game was hard-fought. Tang won the first set 8-6. In the second set, Hu's strength waned, and he was helpless, losing 6-0 to Tang.

Starting at 4:30 PM was the open singles semi-final. Carlson is a champion in Shanghai, and Fox is also a veteran of many years, with added stability. Carlson's victory was expected, but the two were fiercely competitive. Carlson's sharp and decisive left and right shots were met by Fox's calm response and fierce returns, making the performance quite exciting. However, the situation was entirely controlled by Carlson, so he won in straight sets, losing only five games.

The other open semi-final was Kola vs. Luo Min'e, the only remaining Chinese player. The two had similar hitting styles, each using long baseline shots, and occasionally going to the net. Kola is a first-class player in Shanghai, known for his steady play, correct ball placement, and few errors. Luo tried his best, but was no match for him. Kola won the first two sets with two 6-2 victories. In the third set, Kola was ahead 5-3, but Luo Min'e suddenly rallied, using steady and fierce shots to make Kola tired, and won the set 8-6. In the fifth set, Luo Min'e was leading 3-1, but Kola won five consecutive games to end the match.

Education News

Ministry of Education Announces

Revised Primary School Regulations

(Central News Agency, Nanjing, 25th) The Ministry of Education announced the revised primary school regulations on the 25th. This revision is based on the results of research opinions from education authorities in various provinces and cities, and detailed整理 of the implementation experience of primary schools in recent years. Articles on the appointment, treatment, and protection of primary school teachers have been added, and places that overlap with other regulations have been reduced. There are 14 main points of the revision, and the most important ones are recorded as follows: (1) Regarding short-term primary schools, the Ministry of Education has separately formulated provisional regulations for one-year short-term primary schools and abolished the two implementation methods of the first phase of implementing compulsory education and short-term compulsory education. Now, this article is appropriately revised and regulations for simplified primary schools are stipulated, which will be formulated by the educational administrative authorities of each province and city and submitted to the Ministry for record. (2) Hygiene expenses are added to the allocation of primary school operating expenses. (3) The teaching subjects and weekly teaching hours of primary schools are listed according to the revised and promulgated version in February of this year. (4) Local teaching materials in various places may be edited by the主管 educational authorities and schools. (5) The "assistant teacher" regulation is deleted, and it is stipulated that the number of teachers per two grades should be three in principle. (6) All primary school teachers who have primary school teacher qualifications or have passed the examination are now required to apply for registration with the主管 educational administrative authorities. Except in special circumstances, primary schools should only hire teachers after the registration has been announced. (7) The time spent in school by primary school teachers and staff is changed to 8 hours, and the number of classes taught is reduced to a maximum of 240 minutes. (8) Teachers who are dismissed without reason may submit reasons and submit them to the主管 educational authorities for verification and correction. (9) The appointment, treatment, and protection of kindergarten directors and teachers shall be subject to the various regulations regarding primary school teachers and staff. (10) Teachers and staff shall not advance or retreat with the change of principals or主管 educational administrative personnel.
