*The Shanghai News Extra, Amateur Weekly - Overseas Postal Agency Taiwan People’s Life Survey*

Lin Wenhuan

Xiamen Correspondence

Even a person skilled in dialects rarely masters the Fujian dialects well. Although the commonly spoken Fujian dialect is broadly divided into only two types, namely Fuzhou dialect and Xiamen dialect, in southern Fujian, except for Xiamen dialect which is somewhat passable in a few large cities, almost every county, even every two towns, has its own dialect. However, the Taiwanese people from that foreign land all use the Xiamen dialect of southern Fujian. Because of the ease of communication, southern Fujian has become a gathering place and refuge for Taiwanese people.

Since Xiamen was opened as a commercial port, it has become the gateway to the Zhangjiang River in southern Fujian, and goods are gathered here. As a result, overseas Chinese gather, people from all directions mix, and the market flourishes daily. Everywhere, there is a custom that once a place becomes prosperous, gambling dens and brothels will emerge in response. This is also the case in Xiamen. The difference is that in Xiamen, the operation of these businesses seems to be monopolized by Taiwanese vagrants.

Of course, there are many Taiwanese people in Xiamen and Gulangyu who operate legitimate businesses, such as banks, hospitals, and hotels, but they are ultimately not as numerous as those engaged in gambling and other such businesses. In Xiamen city, there is a famous "Taiwanese Street," which is named similarly to the "Chinatowns" in various parts of America. According to local terminology, it is called "Ju Kou Street" (close to the newly opened Zhongshan Road). On the surface, no one can see that Ju Kou Street is a place for "hiding dirt and harboring filth." For example, a fine and beautifully decorated cafe may have a place upstairs for opium addicts to indulge. The simplicity and squalor in between are thought by many who have been to Shanghai to be no less than Shanghai's Swallow's Nest (a reference to opium dens). Sometimes, a magnificent mansion seems to be bustling with guests, but who knows that it is actually a gambling den doing thriving business. Those who are well-dressed and come from afar are nothing more than gamblers seeking the foul odor. Brothels do not openly solicit customers with signs. On the surface, almost all of them look like residential houses. But once night falls and the lights come on, singing and dancing are inevitable, and couples everywhere are a common sight.

That street, like Macau between southern China's Guangdong and Hong Kong, and Monte Carlo in Switzerland's World Park, is not restricted by any authorities or government orders, because the people who run these businesses are very respectable families. They can often stand on equal footing with people in officialdom. It is said that there are three famous Taiwanese clans in Xiamen: the Li clan, which is the most prominent of the three, with widespread influence and abundant capital; the Lin clan, which mainly operates dance halls and cafes, and cultivates relationships with officials and gentry, excelling in social skills and wielding great influence in southern Fujian; and the Gao clan, which is in a relatively weak position and cannot compare with the Li and Lin clans.

The above three clans actually hold the power of the trading center of Xiamen, especially recently. This is because the three clans are all local Taiwanese and also citizens under the protection of a strong country. The followers they gather are mostly fugitives from Taiwan who have fled to Xiamen, all of whom are capable and cunning, and experienced in navigating the world. In addition to engaging in business, they also provide various kinds of protection for others. For example, if someone needs to borrow a signboard to engage in "special trade," they only need to contact them, and they can often save a lot of expenses and get real protection. Therefore, their followers are increasing day by day.

There are even more vagrants among the Taiwanese, and their character is even lower than that of the people engaged in "special trade." Therefore, they do not hesitate to sell arms and aid bandits. It is said that a capable vagrant can buy enough quick-firing guns for a newly formed army in one day.

Some of the more noble Taiwanese women marry foreign businessmen or become their concubines. Those of middle rank, if they are kind, assist their husbands in running legitimate businesses; if they are cunning, they serve as assistants in "special trade." The lowest of them sell songs and engage in prostitution everywhere, without shame. Among them, there is also a kind of "female troupe street opera" that still retains the remnants of feudal society.

Every year in mid-July of the lunar calendar, during the so-called "Zhongyuan Festival," people in Xiamen, like elsewhere, are busy collecting money to hold a Taiping Gong Jiao (a religious ceremony). Paper money and paper clothes are hung everywhere in the streets, fluttering in the wind. At night, each household takes turns inviting "female troupes" to perform opera, sometimes all night long. The operas performed are mostly "Liang Shanbo and Zhu Yingtai" and other stories popular among the Chinese people, but the performers are all Taiwanese women.

It seems to have become a habit. People in Xiamen often treat this "Taiwanese opera" as their local tune. Whether old or young, male or female, if they have nothing to do, they always hum this tune. Of course, most of these operas cannot escape the old Chinese plot of "miss gives gold in the back garden, and the fallen young master becomes the top scholar," but the people who sing these street operas are not the people of China. They have become the whipped subjects of a strong neighbor. Therefore, the sad and beautiful singing often makes people think of the Tang Dynasty poet's lines: "The merchant girl does not know the sorrow of a conquered nation, and still sings the 'Backyard Flower' across the river!"

The total number of Taiwanese living in Xiamen is about 50,000 to 60,000, and more are still entering this year. Because the reporter has many Taiwanese friends, I am often invited to Ju Kou Street to peek at the mysterious arrangements. Now, let's talk about gambling first.

Their gambling method can be described as unique, called "Twelve Varieties" gambling. The twelve varieties are: White King, White Minister, White Elephant, Black King, Black Minister, Black Elephant, White Chariot, White Horse, White Cannon, Black Chariot, Black Horse, Black Cannon, similar to the twelve symbols of chess pieces. The opening treasure place in the gambling den does not gather many gamblers. Only a few new entrants often go to see the lottery in person. The rest, those who want to gamble only need to know the names of the twelve varieties, stay at home, prepare the gambling capital, and wrap the amount of money they want to gamble in a paper package. The paper package also includes their guess of a certain variety (for example, if guessing Black Cannon, specify gambling three corners of money on Black Cannon). Naturally, a runner specially assigned by the gambling den will come to collect it (Editor's note: quite like the Shanghai flower meeting telephone form). If the lottery is Black Cannon, then the three corners of money paid for guessing Black Cannon wins the lottery, and you can get back three yuan and three corners. (Three yuan is the winning money, and three corners is the principal, seeing one paying ten). When drawing the lottery, the twelve varieties are also sealed and randomly drawn to be opened, and the lottery can be drawn in batches (for example, once the first batch of runners returns, the lottery is drawn once; then the second batch is drawn again). The runners can take money from both sides. For example, the runner receives money from the customer and delivers it to the gambling den, and can deduct one corner from each yuan as a fare reward. If you win the lottery, you can also ask the customer for a reward bonus of one corner per yuan. If the customer's gambling capital is large (assuming it is several hundred yuan) and wins several thousand yuan, then the hundreds of yuan of capital spent will all be given to the runner. At the same time, most of the runners are accomplices of the gambling den boss. When they find that many people are guessing a certain "variety", they will inform the boss to pay attention, and some gambling dens even cheat to harm customers.

But in Xiamen, "Twelve Varieties" gambling has become a major event in daily life. Almost every family has one or two people who are addicted to "Twelve Varieties" gambling as if their lives depended on it, and some even make a desperate bet, resulting in bankruptcy.

Not only people from Xiamen, but also many people from Quanzhou, Zhangzhou, and northern Fujian treat Ju Kou Street in Xiamen as a den of consumption, especially those from northern Fujian who specialize in becoming officials come the most. Although it is only a small place, the evils of the city are already very obvious.

Taiwanese brothels sometimes have close relationships with hotels and cafes. If you discuss it with the old waiter in the hotel, you can find your way; if there are female attendants in the cafe, then there is some meaning. Often, dance hall-style cafes also have brothel and hotel facilities; larger ones also have gambling den facilities (sometimes there are also Fan-Tan and Pai Gow games). As for the source of prostitutes, there are the following types:

1. Adopted daughters: The nature of adopted daughters is no different from keeping maids. When they are young, they specialize in doing chores and are slaves in the family. When they reach the age of twelve or thirteen, their treatment is divided according to their beauty. The beautiful ones become money trees for the brothel, and the rest are either sold to other places or transferred to female opera troupes, etc., and some are maids in the brothel for life. However, when the madam starts buying adopted daughters, they are mostly around ten years old, and their appearance will not change too much, so there are very few ugly ones.

2. Those who are lured and abducted: There are also women who are lured into brothels through tricks. Many are abducted and sold into brothels. Most of those who are older belong to this category.

3. Those who are pawned: There are also those whose parents or daughters-in-law, or wives with husbands, pawned into the brothel as prostitutes due to economic difficulties, mostly with a pawn period of three to five years. Pawning is like selling, but they can be redeemed when they have money. Because people can generate profits, no interest is charged on the money obtained from pawning.

Most of the female actors in female opera troupes are pawned.

Opium is entirely smuggled. It is said that in addition to importing from southwest Fujian, some are also brought in by sea ships. Most of the opium den bosses are Taiwanese, or they have to borrow a signboard. The locations are mostly upstairs in cafes; some are in hotels; some are in gambling dens. Gamblers in gambling dens can smoke for free (including opium, cigars, cigarettes, etc.).

Ju Kou Street is not only a gathering place for dismissed dignitaries from Fujian Province, but also inevitably a place for bandits to relax. Fujian Province is famous for its people's army; but the so-called people's army, if not recruited by the central government, is of course still bandits. Therefore, Ju Kou Street is not only a refuge for Taiwanese fugitives, but also a refuge for Fujianese fugitives.

There are also many tragic killings in Ju Kou Street, and the expansion and disappearance of events are often unexpected. If we want to describe Ju Kou Street, we can call it one of the "special zones."

However, the upper and lower classes of Xiamen city secretly regard Ju Kou Street as the trend, influencing them. If we think about the local community, we will feel that it is a fire-breathing mouth that destroys Xiamen.

Book Review: Zhang Yihong's "Introduction to Philosophy" 134

Liangfu

(This book was recently published by Xin Ken Bookstore, priced at 9 corners)

There are many books on the introduction to philosophy that can be found in bookstores. Some are written by themselves, some are translated from Western Europe, and some are compiled based on other people's books. However, generally speaking, they are all inherited and transcribed, a set of old philosophical systems, without new opinions. After reading this kind of introduction to philosophy, we feel as if they are all the same, without any new content. Originally, this kind of introductory book on philosophy did not give us specific content of the current new philosophy, nor did it use advanced new philosophical research methods, but only talked about ontology, cosmology, and philosophy of life, etc., the empty framework of decadent and dead philosophy, listing some opinions from old philosophical schools such as monotheism, polytheism, dogmatism, and skepticism. It does not stand on the standpoint of new philosophy and specifically grasp the content of the living philosophy of the present.

Recently, a book "Introduction to Philosophy" by Zhang Yihong was published. In recent years, no one has written books on the introduction to philosophy. Perhaps people who study philosophy, in the old aspects, feel that the previous philosophical system is enough, and there is no need to establish another one; in the new aspects, they either feel the difficulty of changing the strings and becoming a unique style, or they think that the new philosophy outlines discussed by the predecessors are complete, and there is no need to follow the same pattern. Therefore, Zhang Yihong's "Introduction to Philosophy" is now considered to have broken this silence of many years.

Naturally, this "Introduction to Philosophy" also has its own unique features. For example, many other books only discuss the opinions of various schools in the idealism school, such as monotheism, polytheism, etc., and never mention materialism, let alone dialectical materialism. This shows that they are completely old philosophical introductions to philosophy, idealistic introductions to philosophy, and introductions to philosophy of the past. It is by no means a truly current introduction to philosophy.

But

Page 20

Now in our book, although the system also inherits the arrangement of the old introduction to philosophy, after all, at the end of each chapter or section, when describing the opinions of various schools, it also puts forward the emerging materialism, and does not let the philosophical opinions of idealism completely occupy the entire field of the introduction to philosophy, but also raises the new materialism to compete with idealism, sharing the world equally. This point is what makes this book different from other introductions to philosophy, and also shows the author's attention to dialectical materialism or bias towards dialectical materialism.

However, we think that this is still not enough. According to the consistent method of this book, in discussing each opinion, it only describes the statements of various schools, and then uses dialectical materialism to unify it. It seems that all opinions have their own merits, and should be permanently preserved, encompassing all, and stored in new materialism. Moreover, in many places, it does not express its own opinions at all, but only, like old philosophers, completely lists and elaborates the opinions of various schools, providing some materials, without making choices and criticisms. Based on these, we know that the author's standpoint is only intentionally or unintentionally and unconsciously aware of dialectical materialism, and has not resolutely stood on the standpoint of new materialism to criticize all the opinions of the previous old philosophy. He only wants to unify, compromise, and reconcile: he ignores overcoming and negating.

Another thing is about the style. Naturally, the form is determined by the content. Because this book cannot completely escape the system of the old introduction to philosophy, it still divides the connotation of philosophy into several departments: epistemology, cosmology, ontology, and philosophy of life. Although the author said in this book, "Ontology and cosmology are unified in natural philosophy," "Called natural philosophy, it is equivalent to natural science," and "Philosophy of life (philosophy of life—author's note) is the content of social science," but despite saying this, the system of this introduction to philosophy still lists ontology, cosmology, and philosophy of life. I think the author of this book has also read Engels's works, right? Didn't Engels clearly say: "After understanding the achievements of the development of philosophy for two thousand five hundred years, natural science, on the one hand, can break away from special natural philosophy, stand apart from it, and above it..." He also said: "Because of the great progress of natural philosophy,... we can use the materials provided by empirical natural science itself to create a chart of the interconnections of all natural phenomena. ...Now people only need to observe the results obtained by studying nature with the dialectical method, that is, the results obtained by studying the interconnections between various natural processes, and they can get a natural system that is enough for the present era,... so natural philosophy is also definitely eliminated." So natural philosophy "equivalent to natural science", that is, what Mr. Zhang called ontology and cosmology, "is also definitely eliminated." Engels also said: "This historical view (materialist historical view) resulted in the philosophy of the entire history, just as the dialectical view of nature made all philosophy of nature useless and impossible." Then, is there still room for the philosophy of life, which is "the content of social science"? Therefore, "after philosophy is driven out of nature and history, only one area is left for it to hide. This area is pure thought: the study of the laws of thought—logic and dialectics." And dialectics is the general law of the movement of nature, society, and thinking, so the task of philosophy now is to study this point. The specific content is dialectical materialism and the dialectics of materialism. What ontology, cosmology, and philosophy of life are all the content of the old philosophical introduction to philosophy. This is what the author of this book does not understand, and it is also the place where it falls into the same old rut as the old philosophy.

However, although the author still raises the philosophy of life and natural philosophy in the old philosophy above the introduction to philosophy, when he talks about the direction of philosophy, he concludes that the elimination of philosophy is the same as many people who advocate the elimination of philosophy before and now. If you understand what the previous philosophies were, and understand what the content of the current philosophy is, then I think you will know that new philosophy has its own special area, which is the study of "logic and dialectics." Perhaps this point is also Mr. Zhang's overcorrection? Engels only said that the former natural philosophy and historical philosophy "have been eliminated", and "classical philosophy" has reached "the end", and never said that new philosophy, "logic and dialectics" has reached the end. When Mr. Zhang wants to elaborate on the content of philosophy, he does not hesitate to pull in the natural philosophy and philosophy of life that have been eliminated from classical philosophy. When he wants to negate philosophy, he even drives out the logic and dialectics that "leave one place for it to hide", then why did Mr. Zhang have to do this introduction to philosophy? According to the former, there is already an old introduction to philosophy, why make another one? According to the latter, there is no philosophy, where does the introduction to philosophy come from?

The above are just two main opinions that I disagree with about this book, which are also two important points in this book. As for other details, there are many things worth discussing, but I can't say more here. However, compared with the general introduction to philosophy in bookstores, this book is more neat and popular for general readers; its arrangement is clear, and the distribution is even, which are its merits. Moreover, it also slightly points out some new philosophy and has the intention of guiding readers to be biased towards it, which can be regarded as the most characteristic place of this book.

A Tour of the Old Palace in Turkey 135

He Rongzong

Istanbul Correspondence

Istanbul, formerly known as Constantinople, is the old capital of Turkey. It faces Scutari across the famous Bosphorus Strait. Because this strait is the throat of the Black Sea and the Mediterranean Sea, and the main transportation route between Europe and Asia, Istanbul and Scutari are very important in terms of terrain. After the war, the Lausanne Treaty stipulated that the Bosphorus Strait and the Dardanelles Strait should be demilitarized and the straits should be managed by a special international committee. The Montreux Conference, which has recently attracted the attention of people all over the world, discussed Turkey's request to fortify the straits. At present, the Turkish people here are eagerly hoping that the straits will be fortified, their rights will be recovered, and the old appearance of Istanbul and the Bosphorus Strait will be restored.

But what is the general situation of Istanbul?

Seen from a sea ship, Istanbul is very beautiful and magnificent; especially at night, under the illumination of brilliant electric lights on layers of modern buildings, it looks a bit like Hong Kong. But when you land and walk into this city, everything will make you feel disappointed. Many of the streets here are very narrow and unclean, almost completely different from modern big cities; in the hotel, especially in summer, the first to get close to you are bedbugs and fleas, making you unable to sleep all night.

Most people here have a strange superstition, that is, they believe that dogs and many animals are servants of God, and they must be well raised, otherwise they will be punished by God. It is said that there were very many dogs here for a period of time, until after the outbreak of the war, the British army captured hundreds of thousands of dogs and exiled them to a lonely island in Marmara; this island was later called Big Island. Now there are indeed very few dogs here, but there are very many cats, and you can hear the sound of meowing almost everywhere, and you can smell the stench of cat feces everywhere; this may be because cats have not encountered a large-scale investigation that catches them all in one go.

However, Istanbul also has many places of interest to visit, such as the old palace, especially the great treasury in the middle, which is rare to see elsewhere. This place was closed in the past, and no one could go in to see it without the permission of the Turkish emperor. From the last Turkish emperor, Muhammad V, to the current president, Kemal, I don't know how many twists and turns it has gone through, and it has finally been fully opened now, and even foreigners can go in to visit at will.

In the great treasury of the palace, which is most noticeable to tourists, there are many rare and precious treasures. The first thing that can make anyone shrink back is the throne of the Persian emperor. It is said that this throne was built in 1501, when the Persian emperor Ismail I was in power. It is made of gold, its four feet are inlaid with countless pearls and gemstones of the same color, and it is covered with a huge crystal cover; it looks magnificent and dazzling, like a treasure mountain. In addition, there is a similar throne, also made of gold, also inlaid with many diamonds, rubies, sapphires, pearls and other treasures. But this throne is not covered with a crystal cover, but a round gold cover, on which is also hung a gold lock inlaid with emeralds, its size is a bit surprising, its end alone is six inches long and two inches thick, and on it is engraved with Islamic scripture verses.

When we stare at these two thrones, we always want to reach out and touch them, we always want to move them to ourselves; sometimes we even can't help but want to sit on them and taste what it is like to sit on them. Really, when you see such precious thrones, you will have the fantasy of being an emperor; who doesn't want to be an emperor? If possible.

Next to those two thrones, there is a crystal cabinet, in which are not other items, but three huge emeralds and many treasures. In addition, there are also displayed many gold-made and gem-inlaid scabbards, as well as countless armors, daggers, swords, etc., their light is dazzling and frightening.

But what is said above is only the situation of the first room of the treasury, in addition, there is a second room, also called the treasure room. There are twelve crystal tanks in the room, all seven or eight inches high; all of them are filled with diamonds, pearls, emeralds, rubies, sapphires and other treasures. In addition, there are also several large stones, with delicate jade carvings of various patterns or animal shapes; because the light is flashing, it looks like several giant beasts are turning their eyes there. However, I think the most valuable thing here is still the many clocks and watches since the sixteenth century, which can let people see the various stages that the development of modern civilization has gone through; moreover, among the countless clocks and watches, there is a clock inherited from 1740, which makes twenty-four different sounds a day to report the time to people; this is not only a treasure, but also the most valuable thing in science and culture.

In short, there are many precious items in the palace treasury, and it is impossible to say them all at once; if you want to come to Istanbul, I hope you will visit this place first.

Book Review: Introduction to "Literary Circles" 136

Ji Chong

—Priced at two dimes per copy, sold at Guangming Bookstore, Fourth Road—

Recently, the number of literary magazines that have appeared in China is probably more than any period since the New Literature Movement. This is something that every literature lover can feel. What we are going to introduce now is the "Literary Circles" which is worthy of attention among the many newly appeared literary magazines, hoping that this will enable readers to have a general understanding of the recent Chinese literary world.

One of the newest issues currently being raised by the Chinese literary world is the "National Defense Literature" issue that everyone is already familiar with. "Literary Circles" is discussing and practicing this issue with the most space. For example, He Jiahua's "My Views on the United Problem of the Literary and Art Circles," Zhou Yang's "On National Defense Literature," Zhou Muzhai's "Water Margin and National Defense Literature" in the inaugural issue, and Guo Moruo's "National Defense, Dirty Pool, Purgatory," Ai Siqi's "New Situation and Literary Tasks, Lu Xun's "On Our Current Literary Movement," Mao Dun's "On Our Current Literary Movement," Huang Feng's "National Defense Literature in the Soviet Union" and other papers in the second issue are all establishing and developing the theory of national defense literature. In terms of creation, the ideological content of most works can be said to be the consciousness of national defense literature. In this way, if you want to ask about the characteristics of "Literary Circles", the first is the promotion and establishment of national defense literature.

Among those papers discussing national defense literature, there are three that are worth mentioning in particular: the first is Zhou Yang's "On National Defense Literature," which has a clear criticism of the opinions of opponents of national defense literature; the second is Ai Siqi's "New Situation and Literary Tasks," in which the author points out the characteristics of the current labor situation and clarifies the significance and tasks of national defense literature based on this; the third is Guo Moruo's "National Defense, Dirty Pool, Purgatory," I think this is the best and clearest article explaining literature since the slogan "National Defense Literature" was put forward—the author, in addition to giving a general explanation of national defense literature here, also gave a correct explanation of "patriotism": on the one hand, he exposed the true colors of the "dirty pool" style "patriots" who "collude with national traitors internally" and "flatter strong powers externally" and the Goujianists who "sleep on steel wire beds" and "taste dragon liver and phoenix gall", on the other hand, he also pointed out without any ambiguity: "In the current China, only progressive realists are true patriots, and the road taken by those who truly have patriotic enthusiasm is also the road of progressive realism." In this way, aren't all aspects of the problem clearly revealed?

As for the creation of national defense literature, there are Mu Ge's "One Day in a Certain School," Shu Qun's "Sparks in the Desert" and "Xiao Ling," Xu Maoyong's Flame... and so on. Among them, I think Shu Qun's two are particularly worthy of evaluation. It is said that the author is from the Northeast, and the pain of national subjugation has already been actually suffered, so his works can very naturally reveal the enthusiasm for resisting the enemy. The subjects of "Sparks in the Sand" and "Xiao Ling" are also the tragic events of national subjugation suffered by the people in the Northeast and other places, which the author has personally experienced. The anti-enemy thoughts and enthusiasm expressed by this are also very real, completely different from those anti-imperialist literatures that are fantasized sitting at home. After reading these two works, what we feel is that there are no bizarre places in the development of the story, and the appearance of all events is very natural, but in this process, the enemy's tyranny, the shamelessness of the traitors, and the heroic resistance enthusiasm of the true patriots are vividly presented one by one. Although the words and sentences used by the author are very simple, and there are no particularly sensational slogans, after reading it, it can make you moved, excited, and ignite the same anti-resistance enthusiasm. For example, for the satire and condemnation of the "studying to save the country" doctrine, some works in the past have also expressed this point, but those expressions mostly rely on fierce words and theoretical preaching, or fictional stories, while Shu Qun's expression of "Xiao Ling" is due to the natural development of events. The work also tells us that when the enemy soldiers have not yet reached her, a training instructor, Zhang, is talking about "studying to save the country", but when the enemy soldiers have already arrived, she told the school servant to burn the national flag quickly, and a truly patriotic female student said coldly: "Why don't you say 'studying to save the country' now?"" How concise and powerful this is! Naturally, these two creations also have some shortcomings, such as the oversimplified description in many places, and the fast pace, making people feel that the author's expressive power is not enough, but in the end, the author can still be said to be one of the most promising new writers.

In addition to the above, there are two creations in "Literary Circles" that are worth reading, namely Sha Ting's "In the Ancestral Hall" and Guo Moruo's "Sima Qian's Determination", especially the latter. This should be a historical novel, which the author uses to satirize and mock the general powers by telling the story of Sima Qian's efforts to write the Historical Records after his testicles were cut off. Through Sima Qian's mouth, after telling the story of Qin Shihuang currying favor with the wealthy Wu Shi Luo and Ba widow, he said: "Setting fire to books, kowtowing to cattle and sheep, urinating and defecating on the heads of scholars, offering jade belts to wealthy widows, this is power!... If a literary scholar had rich men like Wu Shi Luo and Ba widow, power would voluntarily cut off their testicles to serve literature. How could literature be allowed to be cut off from its testicles to serve power?" I think that even the current Han Wudi and Ren Shaoqing and his like would blush at this merciless mockery. The author is very good at creating historical stories, such as the past "Three Rebellious Women", etc., which are quite famous. Here we can also introduce the author's historical novel, which can also be said to be a historical sketch, namely "Essays" in the fourth issue, "Qin Shihuang is About to Die", which is written better, more vividly, and has more realistic significance.

Furthermore, regarding the theoretical introduction of reportage literature, there are two articles in the inaugural issue of "Literary Circles": Plere Merin's "On Reportage Literature" (translated by Xu Maoyong) and Andre Marlux's "The Necessity of Reportage Literature" (translated by Shen Qiyu). The former points out that the method of expressing objective truth in reportage literature is the easiest, most direct, and fastest, and explains the dialectical path of writing reportage literature: "that is, from practical observation to abstract thought, and then to the objective reality of experimentation"; thus it theoretically expresses the positive significance and tasks of reportage literature. In this

Below connects to page 5

Page 21

Page 22

Page 23

In the middle, there are brief criticisms of reportage writers from Balzac, Zola to Sinclair, and Kisch. As for the latter, namely "The Necessity of Reportage Literature", it theoretically and practically proves the existence significance and active role of reportage literature. At the same time, "Literary Circles" also published Kisch's reportage work: "Secret China" (translated by Li Bo). This author is a so-called "fast-paced reportage writer", and his reportage works are considered to be the best in the world today. "Secret China" here is a collection of many reportage works describing the social phenomena of Chinese reality, and three articles have been published so far: "Soldier Mudi's Yoshiwara", "Sludge" (inaugural issue) and "Child Labor in Cotton Mills" (second issue). It is said that they will be published one after another in the future: this can not only enable us to actually understand the characteristics of the creative form of reportage literature, but also enable us to truly know many "secrets" of Chinese society.

Finally, what needs to be said is the "Creation Monthly Review" and the "Symposium", which can also be said to be a characteristic of "Literary Circles". I would say that in recent China, criticism and creation have been separated, because critics do not pay much attention to the newly produced creations of reality, they like to talk about Homer, Dante, Goethe, Byron; at the same time, writers also feel that this criticism has no direct relationship with them, and therefore do not want to pay attention to criticism; the so-called development of criticism and creation can be said to be not together. Now that "Literary Circles" has the establishment of a "Creation Monthly Review", there should be a considerable remedy for this shortcoming, and it is hoped that the magazine will continue to work hard in the future until the shortcoming is completely overcome. Naturally, this work is a bit thankless, but its significance is very significant: it can revitalize criticism and help creation. As for Mei Yu's several short reviews in the inaugural issue, although they are too simple and insufficient, the author can be admired for starting to try this work in the current China without fear of difficulties. Secondly, the establishment of a symposium on commenting on creation has the same important significance as the "Creation Monthly Review". The "Sai Jinhua Symposium" (sponsored by the Playwrights Association) published in the inaugural issue can be said to be very appropriate in most of its criticisms of the play "Sai Jinhua"; among them, Ling He's opinion is particularly worthy of attention. We hope that there will be more similar symposiums in the future, preferably one every issue, to collectively evaluate newly created literary and artistic works and even newly emerging writers.

A Study of Essay Snacks 137

Fei

Tangyuan

Named Wan, taking the round shape, hoping for the meaning of reunion. *Comprehensive Jade of Affairs* says it was created by the Duke of Zhou. *Kaiyuan Legacy Anecdotes* also says: "During the Dragon Boat Festival, the palace made powder balls and zongzi, stored them on plates, and shot them with small horn bows. Those who hit the target got to eat them."

Sesame Balls

It is said that it was made by Sun Gong Liu. Gong Liu was a chef of the Yin Dynasty, so the creation began earlier than Tangyuan - also seen in *Comprehensive Jade of Affairs*.

Zongzi

Also known as Horn Millet, it is said to have been created by Qu Qu, the prefect of Changsha during the reign of Emperor Wu of the Han Dynasty. One day, Qu Qu dreamed of a scholar who called himself the Sanlu Doctor, who said to Qu Qu: "I am very grateful for your sacrifices, but they are often stolen by Jiaolong. You should use *dongruo* to fill the top and wrap it with green silk," (these two things are feared by Jiaolong) Qu followed his words and made it. Today, on the fifth day of May, making zongzi is the legacy of this custom. However, when examining *Taiping Yulan

Lidu Company Swimming Pool to Open Soon 138

The Lidu Company of this city, after renting a large residence on Avenue Haig (present-day Huashan Road) near Route Maeterlinck (present-day Ruijin Road), has been renovating the existing gardens and constructing a new dance hall and swimming pool on a vacant lot. Designed by experts, all the arrangements are unique. Pudong Middle School Principal Sues Students for Criminal Offenses - Lists Various Charges - All Three Defendants Deny 139

Han Juemin, 39 years old, from Hubei, residing at No. 23 Dongchang Inn on Avenue Joffre (present-day Huaihai Road) in the French Concession, the principal of Pudong Middle School, recently engaged lawyer Lin Qingchi to file a complaint with the local court accusing students Wang Jiayou, Zhang Yuansong, Gong Panlong, Gong Baoren, Hu Yongcheng, Zhang Bingchi, Yuan Ziqiang, Li Wenyu, and others of defamation and damage. The complaint stated that the defendants were students who had previously been ordered to withdraw from the school. On the 27th of last month, around 7 PM, they gathered more than 30 ruffians and suddenly came to the school auditorium for a secret meeting, the content of which was unknown. Afterwards, they posted declarations and slogans, damaging the reputation of the principal. At the same time, they organized a disciplinary team, vandalized various offices in the school, occupied the school building, and used violence to prevent staff members from working and moving freely. The defendants openly assembled a crowd to carry out violent coercion, disrupting the school's administration, committing the crime of disturbing order under Article 150 of the Criminal Law. They also intruded into the school without reason, using violence to obstruct school staff from exercising their duties, committing the crime of obstructing freedom under Articles 304 and 306 of the Criminal Law. They also spread declarations and posted slogans, falsely damaging the principal's reputation, committing the crime of defamation under Article 310, paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law. Furthermore, they destroyed and damaged the office and the miscellaneous items inside, committing the crime of destroying and damaging property under Article 354 of the Criminal Law, and so on. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Deying opened the court for trial. The plaintiff did not appear. On the defendant's side, Zhang Yuansong, Wang Jiayou, and Xi Baoren were present. All three denied the accusations, claiming that the principal had fabricated the charges due to a long-standing disagreement. The court adjourned the case for further questioning after summoning witnesses.

Zhou Enxiang and His Accomplices - Passing Counterfeit Nickel Coins One After Another - Conflicting Statements Suspicious 140

Zhu Tongsheng, from Changshu, operates the Yu Kang and Ning Yuan cigarette and paper shops at No. 955 and No. 937 on The Bund. One morning recently, at about 7 AM, a man resembling a service worker on a ship suddenly appeared at the old shop, Yu Kang, holding 95 ten-cent nickel coins and 5 twenty-cent nickel coins, and asked apprentice Zhu Hengfu to exchange them for banknotes. Weng, unsure of the authenticity of these nickel coins, asked the man to wait for a moment and took them to the new shop, Ning Yuan. There, partner Weng Fuliang examined them and found that the ten-cent nickel coins were completely counterfeit, while the twenty-cent coins were genuine. He quickly returned, but the man had already fled without a trace. He stored the nickel coins and later handed them over to the owner, Zhu Tongsheng. At 10:20 AM, Zhou Enxiang (40 years old) from Tianjin arrived and took out 80 similar ten-cent nickel coins, 5 genuine twenty-cent coins, and 1 genuine five-cent coin from his pocket. He told the apprentice Zhu Hengfu, "Please take a look at these nickel coins and see if they can be used," trying to take advantage of his youth. The apprentice Zhu knew that he was an accomplice of the first man and reported it. Chinese detective Zhao Yongqing and Chinese constable No. 1863 arrested him and took him along with the nickel coins abandoned by the first man to the Wayside Police Station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Municipal Council lawyer Zhang Shizhu presented the case, stating that the defendant claimed at the police station that he had arrived in Shanghai from Yantai on the Lishun ship, selling candy, and obtained these nickel coins. His testimony was very evasive, and he requested a postponement for further investigation. He presented the nickel coins for inspection. Subsequently, apprentice Zhu Hengfu, owner Zhu Tongsheng, and partner Weng Fuliang testified to the events. When questioned, the defendant's statement was the same as the one he gave at the police station. Judge Xiao Xiefen ordered that he be remanded in custody for further investigation at a later date.

Hurricane Warning in Shanghai - Customs Fires Three Cannon Shots - Public Notice Effective August 1 141

Teppich, Harbour Master of the Jianghai Customs, issued Public Notice No. 9 regarding the change of the wind signal cannon at the Customs flagpole to three consecutive shots, effective August 1. The notice stated that, according to the Customs' regulations on wind signal methods, when predicting the onset of typhoons or strong winds, in addition to suspending a ball during the day and a lamp at night, the flagpoles at Lujiazui and Lan Road in Pudong would also fire a cannon once. This was announced in Public Notice No. 25 on December 3, 1934. In order to distinguish the typhoon warning cannon from the ordinary time cannon, it is decided that, starting from August 1 of this year, the typhoon warning cannon will be changed to three consecutive shots. All ship merchants are hereby notified. This notice is hereby issued.

Deaths by Water and Fire - Overturned Kerosene Lamp - A Misstep Returning to the Boat 143

Yu Changfa

Yu Changfa, 30 years old, from Ningbo, residing in Rongjin Lane on Jessfield Road in western Shanghai, was a carpenter. On the evening of the 22nd of this month, he accidentally overturned a kerosene lamp, resulting in burns to his head, chest, and limbs. He was immediately taken to the Red Cross Hospital on Avenue Haig for treatment. Due to the severity of the burns, he could not be cured and died at about 6 AM yesterday. The police chief of the Tangjiaqiao Police Station learned of the incident and went to investigate, reporting the tragic death to the Caojiadu Public Security Bureau, which in turn reported it to the local court for dispatch of personnel for inspection.

Mao Guangtao

The boat of Zhan Youji, a Shaoxing cargo merchant, was moored at the Laiyi Wharf in the Nanshi district of this city. Mao Guangtao, 24 years old, from Shaoxing, a crew member, fell into the river while returning to the boat from the shore at 7 PM the night before and died instantly. His body was recovered yesterday morning. The police station ordered local head Jiang Pingyang to report the death to the court for inspection.

Examination Office on Route Frelupt (present-day Changle Road) - Two Corpses Examined Yesterday - Chen Dongsheng Fell to Death Trying to Save His Child - Cao Meimei Died from Scalding 144

Chen Dongsheng, 43 years old, a lacquer craftsman from Pudong, residing at No. 85, Lane 567, Rue Petit Chasseur (present-day Danshui Road), on the morning of the 22nd of this month, saw his three-year-old daughter, Meizhen, climbing the handrail on the mezzanine and suddenly falling to the ground crying. Chen hurriedly wanted to go downstairs to help the child, but he carelessly lost his footing and fell, resulting in severe injuries. His wife, Chen Zhou, and others witnessed the incident and took him to the Red Cross Hospital. The treatment was ineffective, and he died at 2 AM on the 24th.

Also, Zhao Cao, 30 years old, a woman from Wuxi residing at No. 57, Shoupin Lane, Route Waldeck (present-day Huade Road), had several children. On the morning of the 22nd of this month, around 10 AM, she purchased a pot of boiling water to cook lunch and placed it on the table. At this moment, her youngest child suddenly cried in the cradle, wanting to be fed. She started to breastfeed. Unexpectedly, her other five-year-old daughter, Cao Meimei, was standing on a chair next to the table, watching her mother breastfeeding. She took the opportunity to climb onto the table, causing the pot of water to tip over and spill on her body, resulting in severe burns. Her mother then took the child to Guangren Hospital, but the treatment was ineffective, and she died at 12:45 PM on the 24th. The respective police stations dispatched detectives to investigate both deaths. The corpses were transported to the examination office on Route Frelupt. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court dispatched Prosecutor Song Genshan, forensic doctor Zhang Yan, and clerk Wang Zuyi to the office to confirm the identities of the corpses. They ordered the respective families to sign agreements to claim the bodies for burial.

Lin Fushan and Chen Xianbang - Two Thieves Each Sentenced to Three Years - Wang Zongdao Acquitted and Released 145

The home of Shi Yin, a woman from Dongting Mountain residing at No. 11, Lane 530, North Baoshan Road, was invaded by several robbers on the afternoon of June 2, at 7:45 PM. They pointed guns, prohibited shouting, and robbed cash and gold jewelry worth 80 yuan before fleeing in a crowd. Subsequently, Jin Yangwu, a Chinese detective from the Jiaxing Road Police Station, and detective Qi Fanglian apprehended two members of the gang, Lin Fushan from Tongzhou and Chen Xianbang from Haimen, at the Fuxing Teahouse at No. 169 Wuzhou Road, along with a suspect, Wang Zongdao. The victim identified Lin and Chen as having been present at the scene of the robbery. They were ordered to be remanded in custody pending sentencing. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhong Qing rendered the verdict in court, sentencing Lin Fushan and Chen Xianbang to three years of imprisonment each as a warning. Wang Zongdao was acquitted and released.

Ministry of Railways Sets Freight Rates for Small Boats and Canoes 147

The Ministry of Railways recently instructed the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations to set the following freight rates for small boats and canoes: (1) For small boats or canoes less than 4 meters in length, the freight rate is 4 cents per boat per kilometer. If two or more boats are loaded in the same car, the rate is 4 cents for the first boat and 3 cents for each subsequent boat. (2) For small boats or sampans with a length of 4 meters or more but less than 6 meters, the freight rate is 6 cents per boat per kilometer. If two or more boats are loaded in the same car, the rate is 6 cents for the first boat and 4 cents for each subsequent boat. For boats with a length of 6 meters or more, the freight rate is 12 cents per boat per kilometer. If two flatcars need to be connected for transportation, the freight rate will be doubled. The rates are effective immediately. After receiving the instructions, the two railway administrations have ordered their transportation departments to comply.

Cow & Gate Baby Food, managed by Yide Foreign Firm at No. 10, Lane 126, Sichuan Road in this city, is similar in composition to breast milk and is a well-known British brand that is sold in various countries around the world. Participants only need to find the blue instruction booklet attached to the can of Cow & Gate Baby Food and bring the baby to the Yinming Photography Studio at No. 321 Nanjing Road for a free photo. One photo will be given to the participant, and the other will be forwarded by the studio to Yide Foreign Firm for the contest. The first prize is 100 yuan and a silver cup. The second prize is 50 yuan and a silver cup. The third prize is 25 yuan and a silver cup. The fourth prize is 50 silver spoons, each engraved with the baby's name. The deadline is said to be July 31, and the winners will be announced in the Shen Bao and Xinwen Bao newspapers on August 15. With only a few days left, participation has been very enthusiastic recently.
